line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">}</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 93.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">M/s Ellal Textile Mills Limited, represented by its Managing Director </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">. . . Appellant</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">Artha Rin Adalat, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Dhaka and others </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">...Respondents</span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Artha Rin Adalat Ain (VIII of 2003)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Section 33(7)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">A reading of sub-section (7) of section 33 of the Ain of 2003 clearly shows that if the decree-holder is willing to acquire title to the mortgaged property, it has to file an application before the Artha Rin Adalat, in short, the Adalat and upon receipt of such application the Adalat will take step under sub sections (1), (2) (2ka), (2kha), (2ga) and (3) thereof and will not take any step under sub sections (4) and (5) i.e one open auction must be held before issuing a certificate under Sub section (7) of section 33 of the Ain.  . . . (8)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Artha Rin Adalat Ain (VIII of 2003)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 33</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">Fixation of a date for holding auction on a holiday can in no way be regarded or accepted as an auction within the meaning of sub-sections (1), (2), (2ka), (2kha), (2ga) and (3) and thus to comply with the mandate of sub section (7) of the section 33.                                 . . .(8)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Artha Rin Adalat Ain (VIII of 2003)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Section 33</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">Auction as contemplated in sub-sections (1), (2), (2ka), (2kha), (2ga) and (3) must be an actual auction and not a show of auction as has been done in the instant case. So, the Adalat was totally wrong in issuing certificate under sub section (7) of section 33 of the Ain 2003 and then to issue writ of delivery of possession of the property in question in favour of the decree holder and as such, order Nos.8 and 23 passed by the Adalat were passed illegally and those cannot be sustained and therefore, must be set aside and at the same time direction need be given to the decree-holder to take positive </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">step to hold one auction in the real sense within</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;"> the meaning of sub sections (1), (2), 2(ka), 2(kha) 2(ga) and (3) of section 33 of the Ain, 2003.   . . .(8)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; letter-spacing: -0.3pt; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">For the Appellant:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; letter-spacing: -0.3pt; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;"> Mr. AJ Mohammad</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;"> <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">Ali, Senior Advocate instructed</span> by Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">For Respondent No.2:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;"> Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate with Mr. Shamim Khaled Ahmed, Senior Advocate instructed by Mrs. Shahanara Begum, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; letter-spacing: -0.5pt; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">Respondent Nos. 1 &amp; 3:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; letter-spacing: -0.5pt; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;"> Not represented.</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah. J</span></u></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;"> This appeal, by leave, is from the order dated the 23<sup>rd</sup> day of March, 2008 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.2206 of 2008 summarily rejecting an application filed under article 102 of the Constitution of the People's Republic of Bangladesh.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">The appellant filed the writ petition before the High Court Division challenging order No.8 dated 31.05.2006 and order No.23 dated 23.06.2008 passed by Artha Rin Adalat, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Dhaka in Artha Rin Execution Case No.255 of 2005.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">The back ground in filing the writ petition was that the writ petitioner obtained a loan from writ respondent No.2, i.e., Agrani Bank, Bangladesh Wapda Branch of 11, Ellat Chamber, Motijheel Commercial Area, Dhaka. In due course, writ respondent No.2 as the plaintiff instituted Money Suit No.209 of 1997 in Artha Rin Adalat, 1<sup>st </sup>Court, Dhaka for recovery of the loan money amounting to Tk. 12,77,53,891.37. Eventually, the suit having been transferred to the Court of Subordinate Judge and Additional Artha Rin Adalat Dhaka was renumbered as Money Suit No. 184 of 1998. The suit was decreed on 2.5.2005 and a preliminary decree under Order XXXIV, rule 4(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure was drawn up on 24.5.2005. In due course, writ respondent No.2, i.e Agrani Bank levied Artha Execution Case No.255 of 2005 on 18.07.2005. The executing Court by order No.4 dated 30.10.2005 fixed 12.01.2006 for receiving auction bid, but auction could not take place on that date i.e. 12.01.2006 as it was a public holiday. Then the record was placed before the executing Court on 15.01.2006 and the Court noted that nobody submitted any tender and fixed 09.03.2006 for taking steps. On 09.03.2006, the decree holder filed an application under section 33(7) of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain, in short, the Ain 2003 for a certificate of title to the mortgaged property in its favour and the executing Court by order No.8 dated 31.05.2006 allowed the prayer and passed order for issuing a certificate as prayed for and, in fact, the certificate was issued on 02.08.2006 and on this date further order was passed to send a copy of the certificate to the concerned Sub Registrar. Thereafter on 29.01.2008 the decree holder Bank filed an application under Order, XXI, rules 95, 96, 98 and 99 read with sections 26 and 57 of the Ain, 2003 to deliver the actual possession of the property acquired by it pursuant to the certificate issued under section 33(7) of the Ain, 2003 and the Court by its order No.23 dated 26.02.2008 allowed the prayer and issued writ of deliveryof possession fixing 27.04.2008 for the return of the writ of delivery of possession. Challenging order Nos.8 and 23 dated 31.05.2006 and 26.02.2008 respectively, the appellant filed an application before the High Court Division under article 102 of the Constitution and a Division Bench hearing the same as motion rejected the same summarily by the impugned order. Against the impugned order, the appellant filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.1503 of 2008 before this Court and leave was granted to consider the submissions made by its learned Counsel as under;</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 24.0pt;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">"The learned Counsel for the petitioner submits that subsection 7 of Section 33 of the Ain, 2003 provides that if the decree-holder Bank is willing to acquire the title of the mortgage property they are required by law to prefer an application before the Adalat and upon receipt of such application Adalat will take step under Sections 33(1),(2) and (3) and will abstain from 33(4) and (5) in other wards one open auction must be held but in the instant case without holding one open auction certificate was issued under section 33(7) of the Ain, 2003. Hence, the impugned judgment of the High Court Division is liable to be set aside. He further submits that section 33(7) of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain contemplates actual holding of the auction once and not a show of holding auction and in the instant case no actual auction having been held, the High Court Division ought not to have allowed the application of the decree-holder under section 33(7) of the said Ain and as such the impugned judgment of the High Court Division is liable to be set aside."</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black;">Mr. A.J. Mohammad AH, learned Counsel for the appellant has, in fact, made submissions in the light of leave granting order, so those are not reproduced.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Counsel for the respondent Bank, on the other hand, has tried to support the impugned order.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">From the record, it appears that the execution case in question was levied on 21.07.2005. It further appears from order No.4 dated 30.10.2005 that 12.01.2006 was fixed for holding the auction of the mortgaged property. Accordingly, order was passed for issuance of auction sale notice. Order No.5 dated 15.01.2006 shows that 12.01.2006 was a public holiday and the record was put up before the Court on 15.01.2006 and the executing Court fixed the next date on 09.03.2006 for <em>tadbir </em>under section 33(4) stating clearly that no tender was dropped on that date. It is better to quote the order which reads as follows:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ; color: black; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Ó5----15/1/06---12/1/06 Bs Zvs miKvix QzwU _vKvq b_xwU †ck Kiv nBj| wWµx`vi cÿ †ccvi KvwUs `vwLj Kwiqv‡Q| bxjvg B‡¯Ínvi ixwZgZ Rvix A‡šÍ †diZ Avwmqv‡Q| A`¨ bxjvg Wv‡K †Kvb e¨w³ `icÎ K‡i bvB| AvMvgx 9/3/06 Bs Zvs 33(4) (</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; color: black; mso-ansi-language: EN;">in the order it has been wrongly typed as 63(4)) </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ; color: black; mso-ansi-language: EN;">aviv g‡Z ZØxi|Ó</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">Then on the next date i.e 09.03.2006, an application was filed on behalf of the decree-holder to issue a certificate pursuant to the provisions of sub section (7) of section 33 of the Ain, 2003. The application was fixed for hearing on 23.04.2006 and ultimately the application was heard on 31.05.2006 and on this date a certificate was issued to the decree-holder Bank under section 33(7) of the Ain, 2003.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">A reading of sub-section (7) of section 33 of the Ain, 2003 clearly shows that if the decree-holder is willing to acquire title to the mortgaged property, it has to file an application before the Artha Rin Adalat, in short, the Adalat and upon receipt of such application the Adalat will take step under sub sections (1), (2) (2ka), (2kha), (2ga) and (3) thereof and will not take any step under sub sections (4) and (5) i.e one open auction must be held before issuing a certificate under Sub section (7) of section 33 of the Ain. But from order Nos.4, 5 and 8 it is prima facie clear that no auction as contemplated in sub section (7) was ever held including the one in question. 12.01.2006 was fixed for holding the auction of the property in question but that being a holiday auction could not be held on that day. Fixation of a date for holding auction on a holiday can in no way be regarded or accepted as an auction within the meaning of sections (1), (2), (2ka), (2kha), (2ga) and (3) and thus to comply with the mandate of sub section (7) of the section 33. Further though the executing Court fixed 09.03.2006 for taking step in the matter, the decree-holder without taking any step in that regard, filed application to issue certificate in its favour in respect of the property in question under Sub section (7) of section 33 and accordingly the same was issued. It also appears to us that one auction as contemplated in sub sections (1), (2), (2ka), (2kha), (2ga) and (3) must be an actual auction and not a show of auction as has been done in the instant case. So, the Adalat was totally wrong in issuing certificate under sub section (7) of section 33 of the Ain, 2003 and then to issue writ of delivery of possession of the property in question in favour of the decree holder and as such, order Nos.8 and 23 passed by the Adalat were passed illegally and those cannot be sustained and therefore, must be set aside and at the same time direction need be given to the decree-holder to take positive step to hold one auction in the real sense within the meaning of sub sections (1), (2), 2(ka), 2(kha) 2(ga) and 3 of the Ain, 2003. The High Court Division totally failed to consider the true purport and scope of sub sections (1), (2), (2ka), (2kha), 2(ga) and (3) in summarily rejecting the application under article 102 of the constitution. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; color: black;">For the discussions made above, we find substance in the appeal.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Accordingly, the appeal is allowed. The impugned order of the High Court Division and those of the executing Court dated 31.05.2006 and 26.02.2008 are set aside. The executing Court is directed to hold fresh auction of the property in question in accordance with law. The decree-holder is directed to take positive step in the matter in that regard.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.J Mohammd Ali, however, submits that direction may be given by this Court upon the decree-holder Bank to accept the decretal amount from the judgment-debtor, if it can arrange the money and pay the same. It does not require any direction/order by this Court, because the judgment-debtor can always settle the matter with the decree-holder Bank arranging the payment of the decretal amount.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 24.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; font-variant: small-caps; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">Civil Appeal No.</span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; font-variant: small-caps; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;"> 314 of 2009</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9pt; color: black; background: white none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">(From the judgment and order dated 23<sup>rd</sup> March, 2008 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.2206 of 2008).</span></span></p></div></div></div></div>

class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">}</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 140px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Manas Kumar Boyragi (Poly)</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10pt;">. . . Defendant-Appellant-Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Pallabi Rani Boyragi and another </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10pt;">. . . Plaintiff-Respondent-Opposite parties</span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 45</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 45 of Evidence Act, contemplates that the opinion of the expert is not conclusive evidence and it is not save guard for reading to any conclusion. The facts remains that the opinion of the expert under the purview of section 45 of the Evidence Act, being not conclusive evidence, it can be varied, modified even set-aside after proper analysis of the evidence of the respective parties. The learned court is empowered to give a conclusive decision as to the matter of controversy between the parties after proper adjudication and evaluation of the evidence adduced from the sides of the respective parties. The expert’s opinion is one of the substantive pieces of evidence and the learned court at the time of disposal of the appeal finally can arrive at a concrete decision from all the evidence which is already on records.             . . .(13)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">1978 BLD (AD) 142 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. S. M. Abul Hossain,  Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">----<strong><em>For the petitioner</em></strong>.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Dipayan Saha, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10pt;">… For the opposite party No. 01 &amp; 02.</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Soumendra Sarker, J: </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the judgment and order dated 10.11.2016 passed by the learned District Judge, Pirojpur in Family Appeal No. 12 of 2013 should not be set-aside and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts leading to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated thus, the present opposite parties as plaintiffs instituted the Original Family Suit being No. 18 of 2011 in the learned Family court of Vandaria, Pirojpur contending inter alia that the petitioner married the opposite party No. 01 on 24.11.2004 and at the time of marriage the father of the plaintiff gave the defendant a good number of  gold ornaments and cash money amounting to taka 60,000/= for the purpose of business of the defendant. That the marriage was duly consummated and during the subsistence of  marriage the plaintiff No. 01 gave birth of a child, the plaintiff No. 02 on 27.10.2005. Subsequently; the defendant due to ill advise of his parents demanded taka 60,000/= more from the father of the plaintiff and while the father of the plaintiff refused to pay the amount, on 25.04.2005 the defendant drove out the plaintiffs from his residence with only the wearing apparels which constrained the plaintiffs to institute the Original Suit for maintenance and others.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The contrary case of the defendant-petitioner in short is thus, that the plaintiff is not the legally married wife of the defendant and the plaintiff No. 02 Manik Kumar Boiragi is not the son of the defendant. The defendant denied the paternity of the child and filed a written statement stating that on false allegations the plaintiffs have instituted the original suit. The learned family court after trial, decreed the suit on contest vide judgment and decree dated 29.10.2013.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and decree the defendant preferred a Family Appeal being No. 12 of 2013 in the court of the learned District Judge, Pirojpur. The learned District Judge during pendency of the appeal passed an order on 06.08.2015 directing to conduct DNA test of the opposite party No. 02 with the petitioner and opposite party No. 1 to ascertain the paternity. Accordingly; on 18.04.2016 the National Forensic DNA Laboratory, Dhaka submitted it’s report stating that the defendant is the biological father of the plaintiff No. 02. Thereafter the defendant-petitioner on 11.08.2016 submitted a written objection against the report of the DNA test and the learned appellate court hearing the same rejected the application on 13.10.2016. Thereafter the defendant on 10.11.2016 filed an application for DNA test afresh to determine the paternity of the child stating that the earlier DNA report does not specify the specimen and sample obtained for the DNA test and that the DNA report itself was not endorsed by the higher officer. The learned District Judge, Pirojpur hearing that application rejected the same by the impugned judgment and order dated 10.11.2016.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and order the defendant-appellant-petitioner has preferred this revisional application under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure and obtained the Rule with an interim order of stay. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">During hearing of this Rule Mr. S. M. Abul Hossain the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the petitioner while Mr. Dipayan Saha he learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the opposite parties.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner submits that the learned lower appellate court during passing the impugned judgment and order committed illegality and irregularity. The learned Advocate further submits that the court of appeal viz. the learned District Judge, Pirojpur failed to appreciate that the expert who conducted the DNA test, not properly and scientifically concluding the test submitted his report. The learned Advocate also submits that the learned District Judge failed to consider that the DNA report does not specify the specimen and sample obtained for the DNA test. Moreover; the DNA report itself was not endorsed by any higher authority. The learned Advocate also submits that the lower Appellate court during passing the impugned judgment  and order without assigning any reason rejected the application illegally and failed to consider that locus D851179, D21S11, D3S1358, D18S51, D5S818 FGA do not match with the disputed child who is the opposite party No. 02 of this revisional application. The learned Advocate lastly submits that the learned District Judge, Pirojpur failed to determine that the DNA test report being not conclusive for final adjudication into the matter in dispute is not inevitable and as such the impugned judgment and order is not sustainable. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">As against the aforesaid submissions of the learned Advocate for the petitioner, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the Opposite parties opposing the Rule controverted the argument advanced from the side of the learned Counsel for the petitioner and submits that the learned District Judge, Pirojpur committed no illegality or irregularity in passing the impugned judgment and order. The learned Advocate further submits that the learned District Judge, rightly arrived at a decision that the report of the expert who conducted the DNA test is not conclusive evidence. The learned Advocate also submits that the National forensic DNA Profile Laboratory is the only acceptable recognized Laboratory for DNA test and the Expert Mr. Ashish Kumar Majumder who is a Scientific Officer of the aforesaid Laboratory rightly in presence of both the parties after taking specimen sample from the defendant and the plaintiffs No. 01 and 02  examined the same scientifically and properly and thereafter submitted his report on completion of all official formalities and for that reason there is no necessity for DNA test for the 2<sup>nd</sup> time which will  prolong the hearing of the appeal and final disposal of the same. The learned Advocate lastly submits that there is no illegality or infirmity in the impugned judgment and order by which the judgment and order passed by the learned appellate court below can be interfered with.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">Considering the submissions of the learned Advocates having gone through the impugned judgment and order passed by the learned District Judge, Pirojpur in Family Appeal No. 12 of 2013, along with the  application for holding second DNA examination from the side of the appellant and the order passed by the learned District Judge, i.e. the  appellate court, the written objection filed by the Defendant-Appellant-Petitioner against the DNA analysis report with all other connected papers it transpires that the Original Suit which was instituted by the plaintiff No. 01 was a suit for maintenance which was decreed on 29.10.2013 by the family court Pirojpur in Family Suit No. 18 of 2011. Within the pleading of the plaintiff it was alleged that the defendant is the husband of the plaintiff and the marriage ceremony was held on 24.11.2004. It was further contended in the pleading of the plaintiff-opposite party that the marriage between the plaintiff No. 1 and the defendant was duly consummated and during their weed-lock the plaintiff No. 02 took his birth who is the son of the defendant Manos Kumar Boiragi.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Vis-à-vis; it is the specific case of the defendant that the plaintiff No. 01 is not the married wife of him and he is not the father of the Plaintiff No. 02. Hence; it is obvious to note that the defendant-appellant-petitioner have challenged the paternity of the child and the existence of marriage between he and the Plaintiff-Opposite party No. 01.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the connected papers I find that the learned lower appellate court finding the necessity of ascertaining the paternity of the child decided for examining of DNA profile and for holding DNA examination he passed an order on 06.08.2015. Accordingly; the parties to the suit has complied with the order passed by the learned appellate court and subsequently DNA test was held by an Expert who is the  DNA Analysts  (Scientific Officer), NFDPL, Nuclear Medicine Campus, Dhaka.  With regard to this; the Government of Bangladesh through gazette notification authorized the National Forensic DNA Profile Laboratory for holding DNA examination. The relevant provision is published in the official Gazette, Extraordinary Issue, September 22, 2014, wherein under section 14; the Government has established a DNA laboratory which is the National Forensic DNA profile laboratory, Dhaka. It appears from sub-section (3) of section 14 of the aforesaid Act No. 10 of 2014 that  the Scientific Officer of National Forensic DNA profile laboratory  is officially authorized for conducting DNA examination and pursuant to the order of the court he has taken blood sample and other necessary specimen and also the Locus D851179, D21S11, D3S1358, D18S51,D5S818 FGA  for this examination and after the DNA analysis the scientific officer of the laboratory opined in the following way that, “the defendant Manas Kumar Boyragi (Poly) is the biological father of the Plaintiff No. 02 Manik Kumar Boyragi.”</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It further appears that the learned District Judge in the impugned judgment and order rightly held that the report of DNA examination is not the conclusive evidence and that for the 2<sup>nd</sup> time again same examination will wastage the valuable time of the court, and he rightly rejected the application filed by the Defendant-Appellant-Petitioner for holding DNA examination for the 2<sup>nd</sup> time by another Laboratory other than National Forensic DNA profile laboratory, Dhaka. The fact remains that the scientific officer who submitted his report is an Expert and the laboratory in which the examination was held is only the recognized DNA laboratory. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">13.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Therefore obviously; other than National Forensic DNA profile laboratory there lies no such authentic recognized laboratory from which another report can be called for, which ultimately wastage the valuable time of the curt to arrive at a conclusive decision as to the matter of adjudication between the parties. Section 45 of Evidence Act contemplates that the opinion of the Expert is not a conclusive evidence  and it is not save guard for reading to any conclusion [ Ref. BLD 1978 (AD) 142].  The facts remains that the opinion of the Expert under the purview of section 45 of the evidence Act being not conclusive evidence, it can be varied, modified even set-aside after proper analysis of the evidence of the respective parties. The learned court is empowered to give a conclusive decision as to the matter of controversy between the parties after proper adjudication and evaluation of the evidence adduced from the sides of the respective parties. The Expert’s opinion is one of the a substantive piece of evidence and the learned court at the time of disposal of the appeal finally can arrive at a concrete decision from all the evidence which is already on records. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">14.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Be that as it may; I have every reason to inclined such a view that the learned District Judge committed no such illegality or infirmity by which the impugned judgment and order can be interfered with. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">15.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the foregoing narrative; the Rule have got no merit to succeed. In the result; the Rule is discharged. The impugned judgment and order dated 10.11.2016 passed by the learned District Judge, Pirojpur in Family Appeal No. 12 of 2013 is hereby affirmed. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">16.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The order of stay granted earlier at the time of issuance of the Rule stands vacated. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">17.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">                   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">However; there will be no order as to costs.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">18.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">                   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Communicate the judgment and order at once.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 24.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">4470 of 2016</span></span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
585	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Abdul Jabber Sarder Vs. Atabuddin and others 2018 (1) LNJ 61</h2>

Ziaul Karim. SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 2 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="65" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 1 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="66" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 2 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="67" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 1 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="68" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Dark List Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Grid Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException
